<p><b>Victoria Highlanders FC</b> are a Canadian <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">soccer</a> team based in <a href="/wiki/Victoria,_British_Columbia" title="Victoria, British Columbia">Victoria, British Columbia</a>, Canada. Founded in 2008 after the excitement of the <a href="/wiki/2007_FIFA_U-20_World_Cup" title="2007 FIFA U-20 World Cup">FIFA U-20 World Cup</a> saw crowds up to 11,500,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> the first team plays in the <a href="/wiki/Premier_Development_League" title="Premier Development League">Premier Development League</a> (PDL), the fourth tier of the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_soccer_league_system" title="Canadian soccer league system">Canadian Soccer Pyramid</a>. The Highlanders organization includes a U-21 reserve Highlanders team and a <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Highlanders_Women" title="Victoria Highlanders Women">women's program</a>. The Highlanders also co-ordinated an U-21 Vancouver Island Soccer League teams as a development pool for players ages 16 to 21. Highlanders FC players were Canadian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canadian_Interuniversity_Sport" title="Canadian Interuniversity Sport">CIS</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NCAA" title="NCAA">NCAA</a> Division I University and College players, Canadian U20 National Team Players, local <a href="/wiki/Vancouver_Island" title="Vancouver Island">Vancouver Island</a> players, as well as imports from around the world.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Victoria_Highlanders&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The team played its home games in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bear_Mountain_Stadium" title="Bear Mountain Stadium">Bear Mountain Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Langford,_British_Columbia" title="Langford, British Columbia">Langford, British Columbia</a> from 2009–2011 and <a href="/wiki/Royal_Athletic_Park" title="Royal Athletic Park">Royal Athletic Park</a> in <a href="/wiki/Victoria,_British_Columbia" title="Victoria, British Columbia">Victoria, British Columbia</a> from 2011–2015. Owner Alex Campbell folded the PDL team late in January 2015 due to not finding financial partners prior to the 2014 season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>Marvin Diercks and Dave Dew, long time Victoria soccer advocates, purchased the licensing rights to the Highlanders from previous owner Alex Campbell in early 2015. Diercks and Dew announced on April 1, 2015 that the Highlanders will start operations again and will participate in the 2015 <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Coast_Soccer_League" title="Pacific Coast Soccer League">Pacific Coast Soccer League</a> Summer season.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>. After a successful season in the PCSL where they finished runners-up to Khalsa SC in the Challenge Cup Final, the club started making plans to return to the USL PDL. During the USL Winter meetings in December 2015, Diercks and Dew purchased the PDL franchise rights from the <a href="/wiki/Puget_Sound_Gunners_FC" title="Puget Sound Gunners FC">Puget Sound Gunners FC</a> and rejoined the PDL on January 29, 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Kit_and_colours">Kit and colours</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Victoria_Highlanders&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Kit and colours">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The team's colours are white, black, and gold. These colours are the primary colours for the <a href="/wiki/Clan_Campbell" title="Clan Campbell">Clan Campbell</a> coats of arms related to club founder Alex Campbell Jr.'s heritage. The heraldic colour white signifies purity and sincerity, gold has the meaning of generosity and glory, while black connotes fidelity and prudence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>The badge consists of a double-headed Celtic swirl, <a href="/wiki/Triskelion" title="Triskelion">triskele</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Triple_spiral" title="Triple spiral">triple spiral</a> with a hub of a soccer ball. A triskele is a common artistic symbol used in various cultures around the world, but is usually associated with Celtic art. Due to the symbol's age, the triskele is a symbol meaning a number of different things to different people and there is no absolute, widely agreed upon meaning. For some it is a symbol of the holy trinity such as on <a href="/wiki/Pictish_stone" title="Pictish stone">Pictish sculptured stones</a> or in the <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Kells" title="Book of Kells">Book of Kells</a>. For others a symbol of pre-Celtic paganism representing land, sea, and sky, or the idea of spirit, mind, and body, or the deity <a href="/wiki/Manann%C3%A1n_mac_Lir" title="Manannán mac Lir">Manannán</a>. Manannán is a sea deity associated with the weather and mists between the worlds, uncertainty, the unknown, adventure, and transformation. Still others associate the symbol with the 3200 BCE tomb of <a href="/wiki/Newgrange" title="Newgrange">Newgrange</a> and harmony. Finally others associate the Celtic triskele as a symbol of female power, of the transition and evolution of body, mind, and spirit embodied in the maid, mother, and crone or the cycle of pregnancy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> The hub, the soccer ball, could symbolize the unity, focus, or expression of the three ideas. The whorls oriented in opposite directions could specify balance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Club_Culture">Club Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Victoria_Highlanders&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Club Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ownership">Ownership</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Victoria_Highlanders&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Ownership">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>With the purchase of season tickets, one also gets a membership in the Victoria Highlanders Supporters Board that administers the fan's 30% ownership in the club. The Supporters Board is a democratic registered non-profit society with limited liability, and all money or other assets belonging to the Supporters Board belong to all members equally. The structure is to facilitate a formalized way to provide feedback, voice opinions, help guide the club's direction, and expand the club's membership base.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> Day-to-day club operations are handled by senior club management.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rowcliffe_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rowcliffe-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>The club has a Highlanders Board of Advisors consisting of Alex Campbell, the general manager, two Supporters Board members, and five business community members. The board of advisors meets quarterly to provide insight and input into the general direction, goals, and objectives of the club.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rowcliffe_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-Rowcliffe-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-11">[11]</a></sup> Another 30% share of the club is proposed to be held by local non-profit soccer clubs. Agreements in principle have been signed with Lakehill FC, Gorge FC, and Prospect Lake SC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Canadian_Soccer_News_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-Canadian_Soccer_News-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the US and Canada most professional clubs are just one of many local clubs and community representation on the professional club is not inclusive. Local non-profit community clubs with paid coaches, technical directors, and staff often end up in adversarial commercial competition for facility usage and academy fees for example. In BC, local community clubs are the only full members of the <a href="/wiki/British_Columbia_Soccer_Association" title="British Columbia Soccer Association">BCSA</a> and some clubs use this player registration monopoly to prevent their players from using outside training.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> The professional club cannot have all local players accessible to them to scout, include in their club structure, and develop into better players. The professional clubs basically have their own small youth development system that is cut off from much of the area's other players who play with other clubs and in other leagues. The <a href="/wiki/Vancouver_Whitecaps_FC" title="Vancouver Whitecaps FC">Vancouver Whitecaps FC</a> separate system outside the BC soccer mainstream is the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Soccer_Development_Academy" title="U.S. Soccer Development Academy">USSDA</a>, and the BCSA set up the BCSPL partly to make a league structure inclusive to the Whitecaps scouting efforts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> Generally given the profile of the MLS Whitecaps, BC youth soccer clubs consider the Whitecaps too big to compete against especially given the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vancouver_Whitecaps_FC_Residency" title="Vancouver Whitecaps FC Residency">Vancouver Whitecaps FC Residency</a> programs are not pay-to-play. The smaller Highlanders club also scouts the BCSPL, and part of the reason for community club ownership is to prevent adversarial Highlanders-local community club relationships.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Canadian_Soccer_News_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-Canadian_Soccer_News-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Supporters">Supporters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Victoria_Highlanders&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Supporters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Highlanders are cheered on by members of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Supporters_groups" title="Supporters groups">supporters group</a> Lake Side Buoys (LSB); whose mission is:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>To participate in Victoria Highlanders games as true supporters.</li>
<li>To facilitate and encourage the expression of support for the team by such methods as singing, chanting, and displays of tifo.</li>
<li>To advocate for the rights of all supporters in our home stadium and away.</li>
</ul>
<p>The name Lakeside Buoys (LSB) is based on the supporter's location at Bear Mountain Stadium by a pond and an effort at a light hearted version of the term Bhoys-commonly associated with overly serious supporters of <a href="/wiki/Celtic_F.C." title="Celtic F.C.">Celtic F.C.</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> The LSB is a member of the Independent Supporters Council (ISC). The ISC is a supporters' groups association for American and Canadian soccer fans to share information and work together to solve common problems.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rivalries">Rivalries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Victoria_Highlanders&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Rivalries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Highlanders main rivalry was with the <a href="/wiki/Vancouver_Whitecaps_FC_U-23" title="Vancouver Whitecaps FC U-23">Vancouver Whitecaps U23s</a>. The BC soccer pyramid has been set up with the Vancouver Whitecaps at the top of the pyramid. The larger club dominates the provincial soccer media and recruiting for men and women. It is common for Highlanders players that excel in one season to feature on Whitecaps rosters the next year. The men's first team competes for the <a href="/wiki/Juan_de_Fuca_Plate_(soccer)" title="Juan de Fuca Plate (soccer)">Juan de Fuca Plate</a>, a fan-created competition for BC-based <a href="/wiki/Premier_Development_League" title="Premier Development League">USL PDL</a> teams, against the Whitecaps U23 side (and previously the <a href="/wiki/Fraser_Valley_Mariners" title="Fraser Valley Mariners">Abbotsford Mariners</a>). As of March 2013, the Highlanders are 3-3-4 (W-D-L) against the Whitecaps and 6-2-2 versus the Abbotsford Mariners all time in PDL play. The club also often has close, sometimes heated games with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kitsap_Pumas" title="Kitsap Pumas">Kitsap Pumas</a>, who also started in the USL PDL in 2009. Their all-time record is 3-1-4 (W-D-L) as of March 2013. The Highlanders prevented the Pumas from an undefeated 2011 season with a 0-2 win on the last day of season. Contests between the clubs have resulted in several sending offs and numerous cards.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mascot">Mascot</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Victoria_Highlanders&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Mascot">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Highlanders' mascot is a Scottish <a href="/wiki/Herding_dog" title="Herding dog">sheep dog</a> or <a href="/wiki/Terrier" title="Terrier">highland terrier</a>. His name is Striker, and he wears the <a href="/wiki/Highland_dress" title="Highland dress">highland dress</a>. He has a birthday June 26, where he has a big party with lots of other local Victoria mascots. He wears the Saskatchewan tartan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History_2">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Victoria_Highlanders&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The original intent of the ownership group was to have a professional team playing in <a href="/wiki/USL_First_Division" title="USL First Division">USL-1</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> There have been previous attempts at professional soccer in Victoria. Taking a step back, the <a href="/wiki/History_of_association_football" title="History of association football">history of association football</a> or soccer in Victoria is comparable in length to most anywhere else in the world. The first documented associated code game was on November 17, 1888 between St Paul's School and the Victoria Rugby Club.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-23">[23]</a></sup> An attempt at starting a British Columbia Professional Association Football League including a team in Victoria came to nothing in 1909.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-canadiansoccerhistory1_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-canadiansoccerhistory1-24">[24]</a></sup> Professional soccer teams from Europe have had one off tours against Victoria sides beginning in 1911.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-canadiansoccerhistory1_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-canadiansoccerhistory1-24">[24]</a></sup> From the first games in provincial competition, amateur sides have charged admission for some games to offset travel costs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-23">[23]</a></sup> The first listed professional soccer team was the <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Riptides" title="Victoria Riptides">Victoria Riptides</a> (1984–85). The second is the <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Vistas" title="Victoria Vistas">Victoria Vistas</a> (1989–90) who played in the original <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Soccer_League_(1987%E2%80%9392)" title="Canadian Soccer League (1987–92)">Canadian Soccer League (1987–92)</a> against the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vancouver_86ers" title="Vancouver 86ers">Vancouver 86ers</a> and teams across Canada. From 1991 on the highest level of Victoria soccer was the amateur clubs in the winter Vancouver Island Soccer League and <a href="/wiki/Victoria_United" title="Victoria United">Victoria United</a> in the summer <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Coast_Soccer_League" title="Pacific Coast Soccer League">PCSL</a>.</p>
<p>Five games of capacity crowds at 11,500 spectators, and three others at over 10,000 spectators, greater than those in <a href="/wiki/Vancouver" title="Vancouver">Vancouver</a>, BC, at an expanded Royal Athletic Park watched group and round of 16 games during the tournament. The other 2007 Canadian host cities will all have either MLS or NASL teams in 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> From these foundations and the goodwill generated after the <a href="/wiki/2007_FIFA_U-20_World_Cup" title="2007 FIFA U-20 World Cup">2007 FIFA U-20 World Cup</a>, the Victoria Highlanders were created. The original intent of the ownership group was to build the Highlanders organization up, so that the 1st team would play in the <a href="/wiki/USL_First_Division" title="USL First Division">USL-1</a> that the <a href="/wiki/Vancouver_Whitecaps_(1986%E2%80%932010)" title="Vancouver Whitecaps (1986–2010)">Vancouver Whitecaps</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portland_Timbers_(2001%E2%80%9310)" title="Portland Timbers (2001–10)">Portland Timbers</a> played in at the time. In 2007, this was the second tier of the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_soccer_league_system" title="Canadian soccer league system">Canadian soccer pyramid</a> given that <a href="/wiki/Toronto_FC" title="Toronto FC">Toronto FC</a> was playing in <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Soccer" title="Major League Soccer">Major League Soccer</a>. The award of a USL PDL franchise was announced January 16, 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jason_Gillett.2C_jgillett.40shaw.ca_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jason_Gillett.2C_jgillett.40shaw.ca-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<p>The first year 2009 team had eight Victoria United players on their roster as the level of play for USL PDL was seen to be higher than that of the PCSL.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> In 2009 three other new teams the <a href="/wiki/Washington_Crossfire" title="Washington Crossfire">Seattle Wolves</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portland_Timbers_U23s" title="Portland Timbers U23s">Portland Timbers U23s</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kitsap_Pumas" title="Kitsap Pumas">Kitsap Pumas</a> also joined the <a href="/wiki/2009_PDL_season" title="2009 PDL season">Northwest Division</a>. The Northwest Division has had strong competition since the Victoria Highlanders entered. Since 2009, the division has had a PDL-Pro side with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USL_Pro" title="USL Pro">USL Pro</a> ambition, 3 MLS affiliates, and a fourth USSDA academy (all 3 MLS teams also run <a href="/wiki/U.S._Soccer_Development_Academy" title="U.S. Soccer Development Academy">USSDA</a> academies). Victoria was fortunate to retain the PCSL team as the 3 organizations' locations that have switched from PCSL to USL PDL did not, and there was no increase in the number of playing opportunities like there was in Victoria. The Highlanders and Victoria United maintain a friendly relationship and play a charity match each season around July 1.</p>
<p>In their inaugural season with head coach <a href="/wiki/Colin_Miller_(soccer)" title="Colin Miller (soccer)">Colin Miller</a> the Highlanders had exhibition games against <a href="/wiki/FC_Edmonton" title="FC Edmonton">FC Edmonton</a> in the preseason and finished mid-table in the <a href="/wiki/2009_PDL_season" title="2009 PDL season">2009 NW Division</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/2010_PDL_season" title="2010 PDL season">2010 PDL season</a> they finished mid-table once again while the <a href="/wiki/Portland_Timbers_U23s" title="Portland Timbers U23s">Portland Timbers U23s</a> from their division won the national championship. In the <a href="/wiki/2011_PDL_season" title="2011 PDL season">2011 PDL season</a> the Highlanders qualified for the playoffs and travelled to the SW Division leading <a href="/wiki/Fresno_Fuego" title="Fresno Fuego">Fresno Fuego</a> where they lost 3-1 in stifling heat. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kitsap_Pumas" title="Kitsap Pumas">Kitsap Pumas</a>, winners of the NW Division, won the 2011 national championship. In the <a href="/wiki/2012_PDL_season" title="2012 PDL season">2012 PDL season</a> the Highlanders finished just out of a playoff spot after a late season rally. They also lost the inaugural <a href="/wiki/Juan_de_Fuca_Plate_(soccer)" title="Juan de Fuca Plate (soccer)">Juan de Fuca Plate</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Vancouver_Whitecaps_FC_U-23" title="Vancouver Whitecaps FC U-23">Vancouver Whitecaps FC U-23</a> on a tiebreaker. For a more detailed run down please see Year-By-Year below.</p>
<p>The Victoria Highlanders have forged a partnership with Sheffield Wednesday, the third most senior professional soccer club in England and one of the oldest in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Stadiums">Stadiums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Victoria_Highlanders&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Stadiums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bear_Mountain_Stadium" title="Bear Mountain Stadium">Bear Mountain Stadium</a>; <a href="/wiki/Langford,_British_Columbia" title="Langford, British Columbia">Langford, British Columbia</a> (2009–2011)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Royal_Athletic_Park" title="Royal Athletic Park">Royal Athletic Park</a>; <a href="/wiki/Victoria,_British_Columbia" title="Victoria, British Columbia">Victoria, British Columbia</a> (2011–2015)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Centennial_Stadium" title="Centennial Stadium">Centennial Stadium</a>; <a href="/wiki/Victoria,_British_Columbia" title="Victoria, British Columbia">Victoria, British Columbia</a> (2016–present)</li>
</ul>
<p>The Highlanders when first announced were to begin playing in a 4500-seat stadium;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jason_Gillett.2C_jgillett.40shaw.ca_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-Jason_Gillett.2C_jgillett.40shaw.ca-27">[27]</a></sup> however, the West Shore Parks and Recreation stadium proposal at the Juan de Fuca velodrome in Colwood did not proceed,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> and the stadium in Langford was down-sized to the minimum acceptable size of 1600 seats, 1200 of which are permanent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> It has dressing rooms, concessions, luxury boxes, and the playing surface is field turf. Capacity concerns regarding dressing rooms, field space, mid-field seating capacity, and training time conflicts for the four Highlander teams with the <a href="/wiki/Westshore_Rebels" title="Westshore Rebels">Victoria Rebels Football Club</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Junior_Football_League" title="Canadian Junior Football League">Canadian Junior Football League</a> and other tenants resulted in the move downtown to Royal Athletic Park in 2011. The primary concern reported in the media was lack of seating capacity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<p>In November 2011 the City of Victoria announced it had accepted a bid from a Vancouver businessman to establish a <a href="/wiki/West_Coast_League" title="West Coast League">West Coast League</a> baseball team to become the sole anchor tenant of Royal Athletic Park (RAP) with a permanent outfield fence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> Baseball teams of higher level leagues have used RAP in the past with a movable outfield fence. Public pressure during the municipal election resulted in the facility remaining multisport.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> Soccer has been played at Royal Athletic Park for over a century. As a secondary tenant, the Victoria Highlanders 2013 schedule was front loaded with all but one home game played before the baseball season's third game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-victoriahighlandersfc.com_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-victoriahighlandersfc.com-40">[40]</a></sup> The Highlanders reserves and <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Highlanders_Women" title="Victoria Highlanders Women">Highlanders Women first team</a> home games were moved from RAP to Hampton Park and Tyndall Park respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Club_structure">Club structure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Victoria_Highlanders&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Club structure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="wikitable hlist" style="text-align: center">

<li><small>Highlanders Prospects is a high performance alternative to the BC Soccer Premier League (BCSPL) Vancouver Island Wave Program, Island Keeper Clinic, Reynolds Senior Secondary Centre for Soccer Excellence, EM Sports Academy, World Cup Soccer Academy, United Soccer Solutions, and optional local community club academies (there are 8 soccer clubs in the greater Victoria area).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup></small></li>
<li><small>The Highlanders and Lower Island Soccer Association (LISA) (i.e. BCSPL and Highlanders coaches and staff) have partnered in the L2T Centre for U10 to U12 soccer players.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> The Highlanders are adding their coaching staff and resources to LIWSA's, and LISA's to further development on Vancouver Island. LISA is an association of the 10 local community clubs on Lower Vancouver Island and Saltspring Island</small></li>
</ul>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Club_honours">Club honours</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Victoria_Highlanders&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Club honours">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>USL <b><a href="/wiki/Premier_Development_League" title="Premier Development League">Premier Development League</a></b> Western Conference champions <a href="/wiki/2013_PDL_season" title="2013 PDL season">2013</a></li>
<li>USL <b><a href="/wiki/Premier_Development_League" title="Premier Development League">Premier Development League</a></b> Northwest Division champions <a href="/wiki/2013_PDL_season" title="2013 PDL season">2013</a></li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Juan_de_Fuca_Plate_(soccer)" title="Juan de Fuca Plate (soccer)">Juan de Fuca Plate</a></b> winners 2014</li>
<li>Victoria Charity Shield winners 2009, 2010, 2012, 2013</li>
</ul>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Managerial_history">Managerial history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Victoria_Highlanders&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Managerial history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lake_Side_Buoys_Supporters.27_Choice_Player_of_the_Year_Award">Lake Side Buoys Supporters' Choice Player of the Year Award</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Victoria_Highlanders&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Lake Side Buoys Supporters' Choice Player of the Year Award">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i>The Supporters' Choice Player of the Year Award is completely funded and organized by the Lake Side Buoys supporters' group. It is awarded to the player who demonstrates high integrity and dedication to the club on and off the pitch. As well as an overall fan favorite throughout the season it is awarded.</i></p>
<ul>
<li>2013 <span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada"><img alt="Canada" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="1000" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/cf/Flag_of_Canada.svg/23px-Flag_of_Canada.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/cf/Flag_of_Canada.svg/35px-Flag_of_Canada.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/cf/Flag_of_Canada.svg/46px-Flag_of_Canada.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Brett_Levis" title="Brett Levis">Brett Levis</a> RW</li>
<li>2014 <span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland"><img alt="Scotland" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1000" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Flag_of_Scotland.svg/23px-Flag_of_Scotland.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Flag_of_Scotland.svg/35px-Flag_of_Scotland.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Flag_of_Scotland.svg/46px-Flag_of_Scotland.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Blair_Sturrock" title="Blair Sturrock">Blair Sturrock</a> CF</li>
<li>2015 <span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada"><img alt="Canada" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="1000" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/cf/Flag_of_Canada.svg/23px-Flag_of_Canada.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/cf/Flag_of_Canada.svg/35px-Flag_of_Canada.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/cf/Flag_of_Canada.svg/46px-Flag_of_Canada.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ryan_Ashlee&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Ryan Ashlee (page does not exist)">Ryan Ashlee</a> CB</li>
<li>2016 <span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada"><img alt="Canada" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="1000" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/cf/Flag_of_Canada.svg/23px-Flag_of_Canada.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/cf/Flag_of_Canada.svg/35px-Flag_of_Canada.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/cf/Flag_of_Canada.svg/46px-Flag_of_Canada.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Callum_Montgomery&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Callum Montgomery (page does not exist)">Callum Montgomery</a> MF</li>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Year-by-year">Year-by-year</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Victoria_Highlanders&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Year-by-year">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>On April 2, 2008 the Highlanders announced their coaching staff:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>Colin Miller- Head Coach (former coach of CMNT, Derby County FC, and Abbotsford Rangers PDL)</li>
<li>David Dew-1st Team Assistant Coach (former Head Coach Whitecaps W-League, Assistant Coach CWNT)</li>
<li>Steve Simonson-Assistant Coach, Director Youth Development (former assistant coach Whitecaps W-League and Women's Youth Development)</li>
<li>Bob Stankov-Goalkeepers Coach (Island Keeper Clinic, Reynolds Secondary School, LISA)</li>
</ul>
<p>The Highlanders initiated their scouting and development camps as well as the U21 reserve team during 2008. The camps consisted of 24 – 30 U17 and U18 players, who received two weekly sessions run by the Highlanders' coaching staff. The Highlanders also sponsored a U18 Lower Island metro team.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> An agreement was reached with the Pacific Institute for Sports Excellence (PISE) for the training facility. In the 2008–2009 fall/winter the Northsound Seawolves (now Washington Crossfire) announced a change from the PCSL to PDL, and the Kitsap Pumas and Portland Timbers announced PDL franchises.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> By January 2009 the club had signed 9 players.</p>
<p>During 2009 preseason announcements of the title sponsor and player signings, the Highlanders made public the goal to join <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USL_Pro" title="USL Pro">USL Pro</a> in three years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> Comments by players indicated the club had a higher level of organization compared to typical <a href="/wiki/Premier_Development_League" title="Premier Development League">PDL</a> sides. The Highlanders opened the season on a four-game road trip that began May 1, 2009 against the <a href="/wiki/Spokane_Spiders" title="Spokane Spiders">Spokane Spiders</a>.</p>
<p>The Highlanders won the game 1-0, with the first goal in franchise history being scored by Patrick Gawrys.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<p>The rest of Victoria's season was solid, if unspectacular, with a neatly balanced six wins and six losses across the season, although the season split nearly in two, with the second half of the season much more positive than the first. A run of three ties and two losses to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abbotsford_Mariners" title="Abbotsford Mariners">Abbotsford Mariners</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Portland_Timbers_U23%27s" title="Portland Timbers U23's">Portland Timbers U23's</a> was broken by a spectacular 6–3 demolition of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tacoma_Tide" title="Tacoma Tide">Tacoma Tide</a> at home in early June, a game which saw five different Highlanders goal scorers. A run of three more narrow defeats ended Victoria's playoff chances before July, but once the pressure was off, the football flowed. They walloped <a href="/wiki/Yakima_Reds" title="Yakima Reds">Yakima Reds</a> 6-1 after being 1-0 down at half time, with <a href="/wiki/Jordan_Hughes" title="Jordan Hughes">Jordan Hughes</a> scoring four in the second half, demolished <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tacoma_Tide" title="Tacoma Tide">Tacoma Tide</a> 5-0 on the road in July, and outplayed local rivals <a href="/wiki/Vancouver_Whitecaps_FC_U-23" title="Vancouver Whitecaps FC U-23">Vancouver Whitecaps FC U-23</a> 4-0 on the final day of the season, ending the year on a three-game winning streak. The mid-table fifth-place finish was acceptable;<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="this is opinion. If no reference can be found, change the sentence (May 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Jordan Hughes and Patrick Gawrys both impressed in the goal scoring race, with eight and seven goals respectively, while Gawrys and Rory Hunter made invaluable contributions with four assists each.</p>
<p>The club was successful off the field as well. In the stands average crowds of 1,734, and a crowd of 2,412 for the home opener, watched the Highlanders. They also had a local Victoria player progress from the reserve team to the first team and earn a scholarship to Western Michigan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> Head coach Colin Miller announced his resignation due to an opportunity in Abbotsford where his family lives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> The Highlanders also announced an affiliation with the <a href="/wiki/Austin_Aztex_FC" title="Austin Aztex FC">Austin Aztex FC</a> of the <a href="/wiki/USL_First_Division" title="USL First Division">USL First Division</a> in July 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> The affiliation included a friendly held on September 15, 2009 which the Highlanders won 2-0. Three Highlanders were given ten-day trials with Austin. One Highlanders player. Tynan Diaz, was given a short contract with the Austin Aztex and played against <a href="/wiki/Stoke_City_F.C." title="Stoke City F.C.">Stoke City F.C.</a> on a UK tour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup></p>

<p>In February 2010, the Highlanders announced they were putting their reserve team in the 2010 premier (open) division of the summer <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Coast_Soccer_League" title="Pacific Coast Soccer League">PCSL</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> They also announced the launching of a women's program, the <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Highlanders_Women" title="Victoria Highlanders Women">Victoria Highlanders Women</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> Ian Bridge joined as head coach and Tyler Hughes joined the ranks and was named captain. The Highlanders opened the season with a four-game winning streak and won seven of their first nine games. Portland, Kitsap, and the Highlanders battled each other at the top of the table in the first half of the season. In the second half of the season the Crossfire and Tacoma/Sounders started generating wins and tightened the playoff race considerably. The season slipped away with the Highlanders essentially being eliminated from the playoffs with an away loss to Kitsap. With five games remaining the Highlanders finished winless in their last eight games to finish fourth. Portland ran away with the NW division going undefeated and winning the USL PDL Championship in the playoffs. The Highlanders Women finished 2nd in the PCSL and lost in the playoff semi-final. The Highlanders played a home and away series against <a href="/wiki/FC_Edmonton" title="FC Edmonton">FC Edmonton</a> in August. Jordan Hughes was a Western All-Star in the 2010 USL PDL season.</p>
<p>The Highlanders launched their Sept-March Academy or Prospects program for boys and girls in July 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> The Highlanders prospects aligned with Shel Brodsgaard's Island Keeper Clinic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> On December 1, 2010 the Highlanders announced the women's first team would compete in the 2011 USL <a href="/wiki/USL_W-League" title="USL W-League">W-League</a> and a women's reserve team would compete in the USL Super 20 league.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></p>

<p>Prior to the 2011 season, it was also announced that the Highlanders were moving mid-season to Royal Athletic Park in downtown Victoria, BC from the suburb of Langford (adjacent to the rural District of Highlands).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> The U18 Highlanders reserves finished a UK tour against development sides of Port Vale, Sheffield Wednesday, and Notts County.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<p>In March 2011 the Highlanders announced an affiliation with a Nanaimo-Ladysmith based group to be named the Mid-Isle Highlanders. The Mid-Isle Highlanders play in the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Coast_Soccer_League" title="Pacific Coast Soccer League">Pacific Coast Soccer League</a> (PCSL) Reserves Division (a U21 division) as a development squad. The Mid Isle side will be older than the Highlanders U20 Reserves (who are U17 and U18) playing in the PCSL Premier Division, but younger than the U23 PDL roster and will act to bring more high level training opportunities to the Nanaimo-based Vancouver Island University and other Vancouver Island players.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> On November 5, 2011 the Highlanders announced the season ticket and community ownership model.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Highlanders started the 2011 season by breaking the Timbers U23's 20 game unbeaten streak in the season opener with Elliot Mitrou stopping 2 penalty kicks. In the second game the Highlanders lost a hard fought away game 2-1 to Kitsap when they scored two late goals including a penalty kick. The Highlanders had a relatively slow start to the season, but in the second half won seven of ten to finish in second in the NW Division. They clinched second and earned their first playoff qualification in their last match outlasting the Whitecap's run for the playoffs. On July 21, 2011 the Highlanders hosted <a href="/wiki/Port_Vale_F.C." title="Port Vale F.C.">Port Vale F.C.</a> who were on a North American preseason tour of the Pacific Northwest. Ashley Burbeary finished the season tied for 5th in the USL PDL with eight assists. The Highlanders Women had a tough first season in the W-League with five one goal losses; however, they finished the season with an undefeated streak of 1-2-0 (W-D-L).</p>

<p>As one of the top two teams in the NW Division, the Highlanders advanced to the Western Conference Semi-finals, or the round of 16 in the overall playoffs, against the undefeated 13-0-3 SW Division <a href="/wiki/Fresno_Fuego" title="Fresno Fuego">Fresno Fuego</a>. In front an attendance of 2369 on July 30 under sweltering 36-degree Celsius temperatures, the Highlanders lost a close fought game 3-1. The Fuego opened the scoring in the 10th minute before Highlander midfielder Jamar Dixon's header knotted the game again in the 19th minute. As the heat slowed the game late, Tyler Reinhardt of the Fuego put the Fuego ahead for good in the 83rd minute by blasting a shot from 20 yards out after controlling a booming drop-kick from the Fuego goalkeeper. He earned the hat-trick with a goal in the 90th minute as the Highlanders attempted to equalize.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2012, a two-game road trip to Portland and Redmond left the Highlanders at 0-2-2 (W-D-L). The Highlanders got their first win when they picked up back-to-back wins at the winless Fraser Valley Mariners mid-season. At 2-3-3 the Highlanders released head coach Ian Bridge and promoted assistant coach Steve Simonson. After a tough start to the transition with three further losses, the team ended the season on an undefeated streak of 4-1-0 to finish at 6-6-4 for 24 points. The Highlanders finished one point out of the NW Division playoffs and missed out on winning the inaugural fan-created <a href="/wiki/Juan_de_Fuca_Plate_(soccer)" title="Juan de Fuca Plate (soccer)">Juan de Fuca Plate</a> on the goal difference tie-breaker.</p>
<p>On September 6, 2012 the Peninsula CO-OP Highlanders moved the Fall-Winter (Sept-April) team to the Metro Women's Soccer League (MWSL) Premier Division. The MWSL is based in the Vancouver metropolitan area and also includes the Vancouver Whitecaps U-18 Girls Elite. The Highlanders women's fall/winter team is a partnership composed of W-League veterans, University of Victoria red shirts (reserves), and Highlanders Prospects (U-17 and U-18 players). After another challenging and slightly improved sophomore W-League season, the Highlanders announced that with the Vancouver Whitecaps Women folding, they would return to the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Coast_Soccer_League" title="Pacific Coast Soccer League">PCSL</a> for 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<p>Mark deFrias returned to the Highlanders as general manager in October 2012 after Drew Finerty stepped down.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></p>

<p>2013 Victoria Highlanders season's home opener was a 3-0 victory on May 4 at Royal Athletic Park versus <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kitsap_Pumas" title="Kitsap Pumas">Kitsap Pumas</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-victoriahighlandersfc.com_40-1"><a href="#cite_note-victoriahighlandersfc.com-40">[40]</a></sup> 2013 was one of the most successful seasons on and off the field for the Highlanders; they finished 8-4-2 first in the NW Division and increased average attendance 57% to 1637, top ten in the USL PDL. The Highlanders made a playoff run with hard fought close wins over Ventura County Fusion and Portland Timbers U23 before a loss to the Thunder Bay Chill in an all-Canadian PDL national semi-final. The Highlanders started two 18-year-olds, a 19-year-old and a 20-year-old. Plus, 80 per cent of the roster was home-grown. The players really stood up for Vancouver Island and showed there is good soccer here. Victoria's run to the PDL Final Four was accomplished without a home playoff game after the Highlanders were unsuccessful with their bid to host the regional and national playoffs. Striker Brett Davis was voted the inaugural Supporters' Choice Player of the Year recipient and presented with the award at the last home game of season v Portland Timbers FC U-23.</p>
<p>The 2014 season was a success for the club with several players earning collegiate roster spots for the 2014 fall season. The <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Highlanders_Women" title="Victoria Highlanders Women">women's</a> first team went undefeated at 12-0-0 while capturing the double in the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Coast_Soccer_League" title="Pacific Coast Soccer League">PCSL</a> Women's Premier Division. The men's first team qualified for the playoffs and hosted their first ever playoff game. The women's reserve team earned the double with a league and playoff championship in the PCSL Women's Reserve Division. The men's reserve team finished third in the PCSL Men's Reserve Division and won the playoff championship. The Mid-Isle Highlanders, affiliate club, won the PCSL Men's Reserve Division league championship. During the Fall/Winter season a partnership with UVic allowed a traveling women's team to compete in Vancouver's Metro Women's Soccer League once again while the men's reserve team competed in the Vancouver Island Soccer League's U21 Division. The club successfully hosted mid-summer friendlies with <a href="/wiki/Rangers_F.C." title="Rangers F.C.">Rangers F.C.</a> of the Scottish League 1 and <a href="/wiki/FC_Edmonton" title="FC Edmonton">FC Edmonton</a> of the D2 <a href="/wiki/North_American_Soccer_League" title="North American Soccer League">NASL</a>. Striker Blair Sturrock was voted Supporters' Choice Player of the Year and presented with the award at the mid-summer friendly v <a href="/wiki/Rangers_F.C." title="Rangers F.C.">Rangers F.C.</a>.</p>
<p>The 2015 season started off with a massive announcement that long-time club owner Alex Campbell Jr. was folding the team due to financial difficulties. Campbell was actively looking for partners to assist him in running the club, both financially and administratively. After the folding of the club in January 2015, many local football supporters took up the mantle pushing for the Highlanders to exist again under wither a new ownership or phoenix club. In March 2015, Marvin Diercks and David Dew announced that they purchased the franchise and branding rights from Campbell and will be participating in the 2015 Pacific Coast Soccer League. After a good run in the regular season, the Highlanders finished third overall and clinched a berth into the Sheila Anderson Memorial Challenge Cup play-offs. After a close win against Vancouver Island rivals, Mid-Isle Mariners, in the semi-finals the club faced off against Khalsa Sporting Club in the Final. After a scoreless draw after 90 minutes, the Highlanders scored early into the first extra time half. But Khalsa came back right away with a goal of their own four minutes from the end of the second half of extra time. Khalsa went on to win on penalties and lift the Challenge Cup. Defender Ryan Ashlee was voted Supporters' Choice Player of the Year and presented with the award at the last home game of season v Mid-Isle Mariners.</p>

<p><small>Note: click on the <b>season</b> for the Highlanders season wiki if it exists, click on <b>league</b> for season wiki.<br/>
Note: Juan de Fuca Plate was created in 2012, all previous standings unofficial.<br/>
Note: Canada has national amateur championships (<a href="/wiki/The_Challenge_Trophy" title="The Challenge Trophy">The Challenge Trophy</a> and the Jubilee Shield) and a separate national professional championship that is currently only open to USSF/CSA Division 1 and 2 teams (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Major_league_soccer" title="Major league soccer">MLS</a> and <a href="/wiki/North_American_Soccer_League" title="North American Soccer League">NASL</a>). Since 2008 Canada has not had an Open Cup.<br/>
Note: Playoff qualification format has varied from top 4, top 3, and top 2 qualifying.<br/>

Colors: <b>Gold</b> = winner; <b>Silver</b> = runner-up; <b>Cyan</b> = ongoing</small></p>

<p>In 2016, the Highlanders began their return season to the PDL with a road trip to Bremerton, Washington to face Kitsap. After being outplayed for 90 minutes and losing 3-0, the USL PDL upon investigation found out that Kitsap has 10 over 23 players registered for the club (league rules only allow a club to sign 8 over 23 players max.). Because of this rule breaking, Kitsap was forced to forfeit the match with Highlanders getting the 3-0 win and Kitsap being deducted a further three points due to rule breach.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FLHOF_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-FLHOF-78">[78]</a></sup> VHFC then hosted Calgary Foothills FC in their home season opener on June 15. In front of an attendance of 482, VHFC lost 2-0 on two quick second half goals by Calgary. The club made a road trip through Oregon over the May long weekend to face Portland Timbers U-23 (1-1 draw in front of 6,575 supporters at Providence Park part of Providence Health &amp; Fitness Day with a late second half stoppage time goal from the Timbers) and Lane United (a scoreless high intensity draw from Willamalane Center in front of a boisterous local crowd). Defender Callum Montgomery was named to the PDL Team of the Week his performance against Lane United.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TOTW3_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-TOTW3-79">[79]</a></sup> Highlanders fifth match of the season saw them take on defending NW Div champions Kitsap. In nearly 30 degree Celsius temperatures, the lads in black and white dispensed of the Pumas quite easily with a 4-1 victory with two goals by MF Ryan Dhillon off the bench in the second half. VHFC travelled to Calgary for a two-game road-trip. Midfielder Ryan Dhillon was named to the PDL Team of the Week after his performance v Kitsap.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TOTW5_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-TOTW5-80">[80]</a></sup> In the Friday affair, Calgary was too much for Victoria and recorded a 3-1 victory. In the Sunday reverse fixture, Victoria played with 10-men for nearly 60 minutes due to a sending off by MF Ryan Dhillon and fought hard back to record a 2-2 draw.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Average_attendance">Average attendance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Victoria_Highlanders&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Average attendance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>League ranks are reported from the United Soccer League archive and North American ranks for outdoor soccer from a website blog that has collated reported attendance from the MLS, NASL, USL-Pro, WPS, W-League, and USL-PDL. Leagues such as the CSL, PCSL, and NPSL do not support the administration capabilities to report attendance figures and those that can be gleaned from media or match reports are much less reliable and harder to find, so they were excluded by the website blog. There are a few teams at the PDL level that do not charge for admission for each and every match due to sponsorship arrangements with a business such as <a href="/wiki/Fresno_Fuego" title="Fresno Fuego">Fresno Fuego</a> (3000-4500 average) or a larger parent club (Major League Soccer affiliated clubs).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
